Round 11 Feature Match - Christian Calcano vs. Brian Kibler
-----------------------------------------------------------


*by Frank Lepore*

These are two players that need no introduction. Kibler is a Hall of Famer that places consistently well in a majority of events he attends...which are numerous. Christian Calcano is the next in a long line of burgeoning magic players who further cemented his success by winning Grand Prix Minneapolis merely a week ago. This is truly a who's who battle that leaves the victor with an 10-1 record.


As both players shuffled up, Kibler joked to Calcano, "So, I know you have [Sulfur Falls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sulfur+Falls) in there..."


"Yeah, I finally picked up a fourth," Calcano responded. Ever since he played his UR deck at Grand Prix Minneapolis, a running joke had been Calcano's mere three [Sulfur Falls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sulfur+Falls).


### Game 1


Kibler won the roll and they were off. A quick keep from both players left Calcano to [Thought Scour](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Scour) himself on Kibler's end step. Kibler dropped a turn three [Borderland Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Borderland+Ranger) and found a [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain); Calcano responded with a [Desperate Ravings](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Desperate+Ravings).


The Ranger met a timely [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame) and Kibler brought [Olivia Voldaren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Olivia+Voldaren) into the world. Calcano had no choice but to pass after another [Thought Scour](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Scour) targeting himself. A turn five Silverheart attempted to bond with Kibler's Olivia, but Calcano had the [Harvest Pyre](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harvest+Pyre)...he only had to choose which creature to target. He decided to remove the Olivia, leaving Kibler with the lone wolf.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpana12/Round%2011%2C%20Christian%20Calcano.jpg)

*Christian Calcano is coming to Anaheim fresh off a win at GP Minneapolis.*
Calcano was certainly playing draw-go while Kibler kept putting out threats. He attempted a second [Wolfir Silverheart](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wolfir+Silverheart), but Calcano had the [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) to flashback the [Harvest Pyre](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harvest+Pyre).


"On the old one right?" Kibler asked, confirming which Wolf was leaving


No, on the new one...wait, yeah, the old one!" Calcano responded. "You knew what I meant."



![Rolling Temblor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Rolling+Temblor)

He got into the red zone with his Snapcaster and Kibler took two. A [Rolling Temblor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rolling+Temblor) from Calcano killed his own Snapcaster, but a Second Snapcaster brought a [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame) back to finish off the 4/4 wolf.


Kibler took his turn and played a [Scorned Villager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scorned+Villager) and a [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat) which immediately dealt Calcano four. Calcano responded by adding a [Lone Revenant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lone+Revenant) to the board.


"You have how many cards?" Kibler asked.


"Just one."


With no plays from Kibler, the Villager flipped into a [Moonscarred Werewolf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moonscarred+Werewolf). Kibler declined to attack, presumably to prevent any [Lone Revenant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lone+Revenant) shenanigans on the following turn, but he took four unblocked damage from the spirit nonetheless. The score was now 14 to 16 in Calcano's favor. A [Desperate Ravings](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Desperate+Ravings) from Calcano put a second [Devil's Play](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devil%27s+Play) into his graveyard and a Pillar ended up dealing with Kibler's werewolf.


Kibler landed a second Aristocrat and bashed for eight, halving Calcano's life total.


"You only have so many [Sulfur Falls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sulfur+Falls) in there. You can't just be throwing them away like that!" Brian quipped as Calcano discarded the land to [Desolate Lighthouse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Desolate+Lighthouse).



![Sulfur Falls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Sulfur+Falls)

"I know...they're a hot commodity! Calcano shot back.


Calcano got into the red zone for six damage of his own which also brought Kibler down to eight life. A [Devil's Play](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devil%27s+Play) for one of the vampires gave Calcano some breathing room, but the pressure was still on.


Kibler played his eighth land and flipped the [Bonfire of the Damned](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonfire+of+the+Damned) in his hand back and forth. One more land and he could deal the final four points to Calcano. He declined an attack, knowing that a crack back from Calcano would leave him at two: a dangerous total against any red deck.


Calcano revealed a [Bonfire of the Damned](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonfire+of+the+Damned) for two clearing Kibler's board, and forcing Kibler to use his [Tragic Slip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tragic+Slip) on the Snapcaster simply to survive. Kibler drew his ninth land and when he attempted to Bonfire Calcano for four, Calcano revealed the [Dissipate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dissipate).


Calcano 1, Kibler 0


### Game 2


"Holy crap, Calcano is unstoppable!" LSV said, as he stopped by to check in on his friends.


"I think he even has the fourth [Sulfur Falls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sulfur+Falls)!" Kibler shot back, never one to leave a good joke on the sidelines.


Kibler made a quick choice to ship his hand and Calcano followed him to Paris.


"Better luck to both of us," Kibler remarked.


But it was not to be as Kibler went back for a new five and Calcano stuck.


"I said for BOTH of us," Kibler continued.


He kept his five, but an [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds) made his turn one [Avacyn's Pilgrim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Avacyn%27s+Pilgrim) arrive on turn two. Back to back lands for Kibler led him to an easy turn three Garruk, granting him a Wolf token. Calcano was content playing lands and passing.


Kibler dropped Calcano to 17 then played a [Borderland Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Borderland+Ranger) for a [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) while Calcano played [Thought Scour](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Scour) and [Desperate Ravings](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Desperate+Ravings)



![Thought Scour](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Thought+Scour)

"You have two cards right?" Calcano asked, as he did some tricky math in his head. He was facing down seven power from Kibler's board and an active [Garruk Relentless](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Garruk+Relentless). Calcano resorted to playing a [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame) on Kibler's Ranger and passing. Calcano was at 12 life after the attack and a second [Borderland Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Borderland+Ranger) joined Kibler. Calcano needed an answer. He dug with Ravings once more which undoubtedly helped him find the Bonfire he needed to wipe away Kibler's board. Kibler's field was demolished and Garruk was now at a more manageable one loyalty.


A Snapcaster from Calcano allowed him to replay his Pillar and remove the Garruk from play altogether. A simple [Scorned Villager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scorned+Villager) was all Kibler could muster onto the board as Calcano regained control. Calcano dropped a [Tamiyo, the Moon Sage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tamiyo%2C+the+Moon+Sage) and kept Kibler's would-be werewolf tapped. Another 1/1 from Kibler and Calcano continued to dig. A third 1/1 from Kibler elicited a "draw two" from Calcano as he removed two loyalty from the planeswalker. With no spell from either player, Kibler's 1/1's would becomes 2/2's. Kibler found a Garruk but Calcano had the [Dissipate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dissipate). [Olivia Voldaren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Olivia+Voldaren) joined Kibler's ranks and Calcano was once again on the backfoot.


Calcano had to tap the Olivia with Tamiyo and he was able to counter Kibler's [Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zealous+Conscripts) with a [Dissipate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dissipate). Tamiyo dropped to a mere one loyalty after an attack but Calcano was hanging on. A timely Bonfire for four damage definitely helped his return.


With no action from Kibler, Calcano was once more on the rise. Kibler managed to find a [Huntmaster of the Fells](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Huntmaster+of+the+Fells) off of an [Abundant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abundant+Growth). Calcano had another Bonfire, this time for five, putting Kibler at 13.


"Boom!" Kibler windmill slammed an [Avacyn's Pilgrim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Avacyn%27s+Pilgrim) onto the empty table, eliciting a laugh from the crowd. "Can you deal with that guy? I don't think you can deal with that guy."



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpana12/Round%2011%2C%20Brian%20Kibler.jpg)

*Brian Kibler falls to Calcano*
Calcano proceeded to keep the human tapped down with Tamiyo. "Yeah, I knew you were afraid," Kibler responded.


Noticing Calcano's diminishing library, "can you actually kill me?" Kibler asked.


"Hold on, I wanna check my sideboard real quick. I need to see if I still have [Devil's Play](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devil%27s+Play) in here," Calcano joked but still checking all the same.


"Found it! I should totally have fourteen mana! [Devil's Play](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devil%27s+Play) you for thirteen!"


"Thank you...for putting me out of my misery!" Kibler joked


The two players shook hands and Calcano took the match!


Calcano 2, Kibler 0




---



Round 12 Feature Match - Eli Linzi v. John Sittner
--------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

Eli Linzi is one of those Grand Prix stories that seem to happen every tournament from out of nowhere. Hailing from Hawaii, Linzi is playing in his first Grand Prix and is doing so with some pretty phenomenal success.


After collecting three byes, Lizni faced Luis-Scott Vargas immediately in Round 4. Despite facing one of the game's greats, Linzi won and used that to propel himself into Day 2 and, now, at 10-1, into position to fight for a spot in the Top 8. He's even packing a Zombie deck that has been flying under the radar in the format.


His opponent, John Sittner is a name that pops up from time to time near or at the front of the standings in major events. He has yet to really break through, but the way he's been piloting the [Bant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bant) Spirits deck this weekend, Anaheim could be the performance he's been looking for.


### Game 1


Linzi curved out like Zombies does, with a [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) into [Highborn Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Highborn+Ghoul), following up with an [Appetite for Brains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Appetite+for+Brains) to exile an [Increasing Savagery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Increasing+Savagery).


And right on time, too. Sittner had led with a [Strangleroot Geist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Strangleroot+Geist) and an [Invisible Stalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Invisible+Stalker), which would have looked awfully good suited up with five counters on it. Instead he "settled" for a [Geist of Saint Traft](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geist+of+Saint+Traft).


Linzi, meanwhile, was light on lands, but was able to play a pair of [Diregraf Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diregraf+Ghoul)s, which, importantly, entered the battlefield tapped.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpana12/Linzi%20Round%2012.JPG)

*"Win or lose, someone's dying on turn six," said Eli Linzi. In game one, that someone was him.*
That allowed Sittner's [Geist of Saint Traft](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geist+of+Saint+Traft) to apply some serious beats alongside the rest of his team once a [Silent Departure](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silent+Departure) took Linzi's only available blocker out of the way. Falling to four and with no way to stop the [Geist of Saint Traft](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geist+of+Saint+Traft), Linzi was quick to pack up his zombie horde.


Sittner 1 – Linzi 0


"The games in this matchup are all really fast," Linzi said. As one of only a very few Zombie players here on Day 2 in a field full of [Bant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bant) Spirits, he would certainly know. "Win or lose, someone's dying on turn 6."


### Game 2


Both players started out with their key one-drops, [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) for Linzi and [Avacyn's Pilgrim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Avacyn%27s+Pilgrim) for Sittner. Sittner used the Pilgrim to ambush a [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) on turn two with [Wolfir Avenger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wolfir+Avenger), but it quickly took a [Tragic Slip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tragic+Slip) on the way to the graveyard.


An [Appetite for Brains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Appetite+for+Brains) revealed two [Dungeon Geists](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dungeon+Geists) and a [Tree of Redemption](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tree+of+Redemption) along with a Cavern of souls and [Abundant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abundant+Growth). The tree was exiled and Linzi rebought the [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler) before passing back.


[Dungeon Geists](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dungeon+Geists) locked down a [Highborn Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Highborn+Ghoul), but [Bloodflow Connoisseur](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodflow+Connoisseur) gave Linzi a new angle to pursue, potentially pumping it sky high with [Gravecrawler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravecrawler).


But Linzi's deck was firing on all cylinders. A [Silent Departure](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silent+Departure) virtually timewalked Linzi, bouncing the Connoisseur, and [Wolfir Silverheart](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wolfir+Silverheart) turned Dungeon Geist into a 7/7, coming in as an 8/8 itself.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpana12/Sittner%20Round%2012.JPG)

*Could this be John Sittner's breakout tournament?*
Linzi was able to use [Tragic Slip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tragic+Slip) took out the Wolfir and even gain a few life with a newly cast [Blood Artist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Artist), but a second [Wolfir Silverheart](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wolfir+Silverheart) repeated the last turn and put Lizni within range of the lethal flier.


Facing a 7/7 flier, Linzi's only hope was to play and chump block with a [Demonlord of Ashmouth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Demonlord+of+Ashmouth). However, a flashed back [Silent Departure](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silent+Departure) forced Linzi to sacrifice it and bring it back with undying, but at the cost of his [Bloodflow Connoisseur](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodflow+Connoisseur). He gained a few life and lived through the turn, but things looked pretty grim.


He knocked the top of his deck, pulled his card and paused before extending his hand.


"That's my worst matchup. You're just as fast as me," Linzi said, still with a smile on his face.


Sittner 2 – Linzi 0




---



Sunday, 12:04 p.m. - Deck Tech: Boros with Paul Rietzl
------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

No player is hotter this weekend than Paul Rietzl and his blisteringly fast Boros deck. While the talk coming out of Pro Tour *Avacyn Restored* was all [Wolfir Silverheart](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wolfir+Silverheart), [Bant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bant) Spirits and Miracles, Rietzl seems to have found the right mixture of cards to make Boros really pop in Anaheim.


The core of the deck doesn't deviate much from the standard block Boros lists. Eight one-drops in [Stromkirk Noble](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stromkirk+Noble) and [Champion of the Parish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Champion+of+the+Parish) backed up by [Gather the Townsfolk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gather+the+Townsfolk), [Silverblade Paladin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silverblade+Paladin) and [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider) are all pretty stock and make the deck hum, but Rietzl was able to make a few key changes that he thinks put it over the top.


The key to the deck, he said, was when he noticed players were running the full four [Midnight Haunting](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Midnight+Haunting) in most lists. He had only had three in Barcelona and often sided them out, finding them low impact most of the time. There was the obvious combo with [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider), but beyond that he had thought they were underwhelming.


"I thought, 'What if that was what I was missing?'" Rietzl said.


So he went up to four and started leaving them in even in his bad matchups. It was when he added the single [Rally the Peasants](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rally+the+Peasants) that things clicked, as he suddenly felt like he had enough ways to make the Hauntings especially deadly.


"It just needed a little pop."



![Midnight Haunting++Rally the Peasants](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Midnight%20Haunting&options=)
![Midnight Haunting++Rally the Peasants](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Rally%20the%20Peasants&options=)

*A little pop.*
Speaking of [Rally the Peasants](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rally+the+Peasants), it has been absolutely wrecking people all weekend. At one point Rietzl turned to Matt Sperling and proclaimed [Rally the Peasants](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rally+the+Peasants) to be the best card in the format.


So why only one?


Rietzl said drawing multiples was always bad, and that it wasn't very good in removal heavy matchups like Jund. Plus, with [Devil's Play](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devil%27s+Play) and [Mikaeus, the Lunarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mikaeus%2C+the+Lunarch) in addition to [Rally the Peasants](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rally+the+Peasants), the deck has a number of ways to break stalls or utilize mana flood.


The results have been pretty powerful for Rietzl this weekend. He even had to mulligan to a mere four cards in game 3 of Round 9 yesterday, but the deck's powerful draws let him race through a slower Jund deck before the extra cards even mattered.


The deck also pretty readily translates to standard, Rietzl said, figuring that the mana probably gets better if you swap in some more white Humans like [Elite Vanguard](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elite+Vanguard), [Hero of Bladehold](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hero+of+Bladehold) and [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader) for the [Stromkirk Noble](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stromkirk+Noble)s, [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider)s and [Midnight Haunting](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Midnight+Haunting)s of the deck.


So while Anaheim may be the last hurrah for this block format, Boros gets the Rietzl stamp of approval for Standard as well. If attacking is your thing, give it a whirl at your next FNM







#### Paul Rietzl - Boros


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

---



Sunday, 12:43 p.m. - Top Tables Round 13
----------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

With the Day Two cutoff several rounds behind us and the Top 8 quickly approaching, Round 13 gives us one of the last opportunities to look at a snapshot of the metagame before the end of the day.


So what did we learn with three more rounds to play?


Jund is kinda good.


People apparently paid attention to Brian Kibler and the **Magic** Online Championship Series, because Jund is out in force late in the tournament. Eleven of the 37 decks looked at for this Top Tables (three players disappeared pretty quick) were sporting the Jund manabase and powerful cards. Chock full of removal, giant creatures and the popular [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat)s, the deck doesn't do anything fancy, but it does a lot of things well.


Trailing just behind it but putting up strong numbers as it has all tournament, [Bant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bant) Spirits is still going strong, followed by [Angel of Glory's Rise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angel+of+Glory%27s+Rise) reanimator and Boros or Red-White Aggro, piloted to perfection so far by Paul Rietzl.


And while the Miracles deck continues to look anemic overall, Eric Froehlich has been lurking at or near the top of the standings all day. Remember, it only took one strong showing from a Miracles player in Barcelona to take down the entire tournament.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpana12/rd13Metagame.jpg)

*Round 13 Top Tables Meta Breakdown*


---



Sunday, 1:05 p.m. - Deck Tech - UR Control with Christian Calcano
-----------------------------------------------------------------


*by Frank Lepore*

Christian Calcano is on the fast track to becoming a household name. He took the trophy at grand prix Minneapolis with UR [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets), and he once again sleeves up [Sulfur Falls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sulfur+Falls) and [Desolate Lighthouse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Desolate+Lighthouse)s on his was to his 11-1 records this weekend. We wanted to get a few words with Christian to see how his deck has been treating him and how he feels about his odds this weekend.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpana12/Deck%20Tech%20-%20Christian%20Calcano.JPG)

*Christian Calcano – now with more [Sulfur Falls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sulfur+Falls)!* 
**Why did you choose to play UR Control?**  

I think it has a lot of game against a lot of decks. There are problematic cards, like [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat), [Wolfir Silverheart](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wolfir+Silverheart) and [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel), but if I can find my answers to those cards, I have good game against everything else.


**What matchups is your best? How about your worst?**  

My best is probably the Miracle deck. I haven't really played against it much, but I have more [Dissipate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dissipate)s, and also Snapcasters.


My worst is probably Aggro Jund probably, with [Strangleroot Geist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Strangleroot+Geist). That guy is pretty hard for me to deal with.


**What do you think the best deck in the format is?**  

I think it's Jund. It just won the MOCS on MTGO this weekend. I got pretty lucky against Brian as well (referring to his Round 11 victory against Brian Kibler).


**How come so few [Harvest Pyre](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harvest+Pyre)? They seemed pretty crucial in game one against Kibler.**   

A third is a real stretch, if you draw multiples they're just dead if you don't have a sizeable graveyard.


**So who came up with the deck?**  

Eduardo Borges and Grand Prix Providence winner, James Rynkiewicz; they were in my testing group. It went 7-3 at the PT. I told myself if I come to this tournament, I was going to play this deck.


Christian is on the fast track to a second Top 8 in as many weeks. He has his eye on the trophy and he's in a good position to snag it! Best of luck, Christian!







#### Christian Calcano - UR Control

---



Round 13 Feature Match - Michael Hristis vs. Noah Koessel
---------------------------------------------------------


*by Frank Lepore*

"Nice color sleeves," Noah commented as both players sat down and shuffled up their matching purple sleeves."


Noeh Koessel has had some success in competitive play. He has Top 8'ed a Nationals, an SCG Open, and has cashed at a couple of Grand Prix before today.


"I Top 8'ed States..." Michael commented half-heartedly in response to Koessel's impressive resume. This was Hristis's first Grand Prix and he was doing well thus far.


### Game 1


Hristis won the roll, and Koessel went back for a new six. Thankfully they were good enough. A couple lands from Hristis led him to a [Mulch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mulch), putting one land into his hand and a notable [Faithless Looting](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Faithless+Looting) into the yard.


Koessel played a turn two [Gather the Townsfolk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gather+the+Townsfolk) and made some humans, while a [Cathedral Sanctifier](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cathedral+Sanctifier) gained Hristis three life. Hristis missed a land drop, while Koessel declined to make any plays despite hitting all of his lands. When Hristis finally hit his fourth, a [Huntmaster of the Fells](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Huntmaster+of+the+Fells) made it to the board only to meet a [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley). A [Fiend Hunter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fiend+Hunter) came down to remove the wolf.


But Koessel had *another* Huntmaster and all Koessel could manage was a [Stromkirk Noble](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stromkirk+Noble). When Hristis attempted to play a [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat), Koessel made sure to respond with a [Brimstone Volley](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimstone+Volley) and killing the Huntmaster. A second Aristocrat joined Hristis's team and Koessel dropped to 8 life. He revealed his top card as his ninth land and scooped up the pile.


Hristis 1, Koessel 0


### Game 2


"That was...a lot of lands," Koessel remarked.


"Yeah it was," Hristis agreed.


Both players kept, and Koessel led off with a Champion of the parish, while Hristis dug through a few cards with a [Faithless Looting](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Faithless+Looting). Unfortunately there was no turn two play from Koessel.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpana12/Round%2013%2C%20Michael%20Hristis.jpg)

*Michael Hristis* 
With four lands, Koessel still had only a single Champion in play, while Hristis added a [Huntmaster of the Fells](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Huntmaster+of+the+Fells) to the party.


"Cards?" Koessel asked.


"Five," Hristis responded.


A [Silverblade Paladin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silverblade+Paladin) came down from Hristis, pairing with the now 2/2 Champion of the parish. A [Pillar of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillar+of+Flame) would do away with the Huntmaster before Koessel swung with the doublestriker. Hristis found a [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp) with a [Borderland Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Borderland+Ranger) then gained three from a [Cathedral Sanctifier](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cathedral+Sanctifier). A second Champion joined Koessel's army and it was looking quite formidable. Hristis took four from Koessel's team, but only dropping him to a hearty 18 life. All of Hristis's lifegain seemed fairly relevant in this matchup.


"What the heck is in your hand," Koessel wondered when Hristis passed the turn with zero plays.


Koessel played a second Paladin, followed by a [Fiend Hunter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fiend+Hunter). When he targeted the [Borderland Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Borderland+Ranger), however, Hristis snuck in a [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) for the save.


Koessel sent the team in and the board became a lot smaller for Hristis as he went to 14 life. But not for long, it seemed: Hristis had a [Blasphemous Act](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blasphemous+Act) for all of Koessel's pressure.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpana12/Round%2013%2C%20Noah%20Koessel.jpg)

*Noah Koessel* 
An [Angel of Glory's Rise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angel+of+Glory%27s+Rise) from Hristis would return a [Fiend Hunter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fiend+Hunter), a [Cathedral Sanctifier](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cathedral+Sanctifier), and a [Borderland Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Borderland+Ranger), in addition to the 4/6 flier. Hristis now had a massive eight power on board, and all Koessel could respond with was a Stromkirk noble. Things were looking bleak.


Koessel dropped to 12 while Hristis sat at a healthy 17 life. When Koessel played a [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider), Hristis responded in the combat step with a [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel). A fiend Hunter from Hristis did away with the [Hellrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellrider), and Koessel could not change his fate He did some quick math and realized the game was lost.


Hristis 2, Koessel 0




---



Round 14 Feature Match - Shuhei Nakamura vs. Paul Herr
------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

Shuhei Nakamura and Paul Herr were unlikely to be in contention for the Top 8 at this point at 11-3, but a Top 16 was very much on the line between these two who were sporting the tournament's most dominant decks.


Nakamura, like much of field on Day 2, came armed with [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat) and [Wolfir Silverheart](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wolfir+Silverheart) in the popular Jund deck. So many of the players near the top of the standings were packing [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp)s, [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest)s and [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain)s that there were probably more Jund mirrors represented last round than most archetypes had single decks.


If Anaheim belongs to Jund, Barcelona belonged in many ways to the [Bant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bant) Spirits deck Paul Herr was facing off with this round. It appeared to be second only to Jund in its success this weekend. However this particular match played out, this matchup was certainly played over and over and over again this weekend.


### Game one


Herr had to mulligan his first hand, but his second was scripted pretty close to perfectly. He led with two Hexproof beaters in [Invisible Stalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Invisible+Stalker) and [Geist of Saint Traft](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geist+of+Saint+Traft) right on cue.


Nakamura, meanwhile, ramped his Jund deck quickly with [Avacyn's Pilgrim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Avacyn%27s+Pilgrim) and two [Scorned Villager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scorned+Villager)s, building up to a pretty devastating counter punch. All of that Ramping allowed him to use a nonmiracle [Bonfire of the Damned](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonfire+of+the+Damned) to clear Herr's board an erase any early advantage he might have had. Nakamura even had the [Wolfir Silverheart](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wolfir+Silverheart) follow-up to, pairing with a [Scorned Villager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scorned+Villager), to drop Herr to 10 quickly.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpana12/Herr%20Round%2014.JPG)

*Paul Herr's quick start gave him reason to smile, but a [Bonfire of the Damned](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonfire+of+the+Damned) erased that pretty fast.* 
After the Bonfire cleared him out, Herr fought back with an [Invisible Stalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Invisible+Stalker) and a Dungeon Geist, locking down the Silverheart.


But it wasn't near enough as Nakamura kept the beats coming. A second Wolfir Silverhart made the other [Scorned Villager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scorned+Villager) as big as the first, and when Dungeon Geist had to block to keep Herr alive, it wasn't much longer until they moved until the second.


Nakamura 1 – Herr 0


### Game two


On the play this time, Herr's mulligan was much less forgiving. His mana issues force him to go down to just five cards, though he was able to cast [Avacyn's Pilgrim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Avacyn%27s+Pilgrim) and [Strangleroot Geist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Strangleroot+Geist) early on.


Nakamura spent his early turns this game fixing his mana rather than ramping it, casting both [Abundant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abundant+Growth) and [Borderland Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Borderland+Ranger) That let him drop a fourth turn [Falkenrath Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Falkenrath+Aristocrat) and send Herr to 16 hastily.


Herr continued to attack with his Geist, but had drawn a succession of cards he couldn't cast. With two [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest)s, [Cavern of Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cavern+of+Souls) (on Spirits) and [Avacyn's Pilgrim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Avacyn%27s+Pilgrim), his hand of two [Wolfir Silverheart](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wolfir+Silverheart)s, [Dungeon Geists](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dungeon+Geists) and a [Silent Departure](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silent+Departure) was essentially a blue source away from being strong enough to compete. The mulligan hadn't been good, but his draws since then hadn't particularly helped.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpana12/Nakamura%20Round%2014.JPG)

*Shuhei Nakamura is still alive for the Top 16 after moving to 11-3 on the weekend.* 
Meanwhile, Nakamura added to his board with another [Borderland Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Borderland+Ranger) and [Liliana of the Veil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+of+the+Veil). He even had the [Tribute to Hunger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tribute+to+Hunger) to punish Herr for casting an [Increasing Savagery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Increasing+Savagery).


Still without the right mana, it just took few attacks from the Aristocrat and the [Borderland Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Borderland+Ranger)s to mercifully end a game Herr was never really in.


Nakamura 2 – Herr 0




---
